\hypertarget{namespacev8}{}\doxysection{v8 Namespace Reference}
\label{namespacev8}\index{v8@{v8}}


This file provides additional API on top of the default one for making API calls, which come from embedder C++ functions.

\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
This file provides additional API on top of the default one for making API calls, which come from embedder C++ functions. 

Compile-\/time constants.

Support for \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Persistent}{Persistent}} containers.

Profiler support for the \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1V8}{V8}} Java\+Script engine.

The \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8}{v8}} Java\+Script engine.

The functions are being called directly from optimized code, doing all the necessary typechecks in the compiler itself, instead of on the embedder side. Hence the \char`\"{}fast\char`\"{} in the name. Example usage might look like\+:


\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keywordtype}{void} FastMethod(\textcolor{keywordtype}{int} param, \textcolor{keywordtype}{bool} another\_param);}
\DoxyCodeLine{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1FunctionTemplate_a41c3051fd8bba064a0de7f2d16488d99}{v8::FunctionTemplate::New}}(isolate, SlowCallback, data,}
\DoxyCodeLine{                          signature, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_1_1internal_afa9ea55d792121fba92b4cfc8ef8c9d7}{length}}, constructor\_behavior}
\DoxyCodeLine{                          side\_effect\_type,}
\DoxyCodeLine{                          \&\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1CFunction_ae9826793367bc905e808d05b70fe86aa}{v8::CFunction::Make}}(FastMethod));}

\end{DoxyCode}


By design, fast calls are limited by the following requirements, which the embedder should enforce themselves\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item they should not allocate on the JS heap;
\item they should not trigger JS execution. To enforce them, the embedder could use the existing \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Isolate_1_1DisallowJavascriptExecutionScope}{v8\+::\+Isolate\+::\+Disallow\+Javascript\+Execution\+Scope}} and a utility similar to Blink\textquotesingle{}s No\+Allocation\+Scope\+: \href{https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master:third_party/blink/renderer/platform/heap/thread_state_scopes.h;l=16}{\texttt{ https\+://source.\+chromium.\+org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master\+:third\+\_\+party/blink/renderer/platform/heap/thread\+\_\+state\+\_\+scopes.\+h;l=16}}
\end{DoxyItemize}

Due to these limitations, it\textquotesingle{}s not directly possible to report errors by throwing a JS exception or to otherwise do an allocation. There is an alternative way of creating fast calls that supports falling back to the slow call and then performing the necessary allocation. When one creates the fast method by using CFunction\+::\+Make\+With\+Fallback\+Support instead of \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1CFunction_ae9826793367bc905e808d05b70fe86aa}{CFunction\+::\+Make}}, the fast callback gets as last parameter an output variable, through which it can request falling back to the slow call. So one might declare their method like\+:


\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keywordtype}{void} FastMethodWithFallback(\textcolor{keywordtype}{int} param, FastApiCallbackOptions\& options);}

\end{DoxyCode}


If the callback wants to signal an error condition or to perform an allocation, it must set options.\+fallback to true and do an early return from the fast method. Then \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1V8}{V8}} checks the value of options.\+fallback and if it\textquotesingle{}s true, falls back to executing the Slow\+Callback, which is capable of reporting the error (either by throwing a JS exception or logging to the console) or doing the allocation. It\textquotesingle{}s the embedder\textquotesingle{}s responsibility to ensure that the fast callback is idempotent up to the point where error and fallback conditions are checked, because otherwise executing the slow callback might produce visible side-\/effects twice.

An example for custom embedder type support might employ a way to wrap/ unwrap various C++ types in JSObject instances, e.\+g\+:


\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{comment}{// Helper method with a check for field count.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keyword}{template} <\textcolor{keyword}{typename} T, \textcolor{keywordtype}{int} offset>}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keyword}{inline} \mbox{\hyperlink{classT}{T}}* GetInternalField(\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{v8::Local<v8::Object>}} wrapper) \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{  assert(offset < wrapper-\/>InternalFieldCount());}
\DoxyCodeLine{  \textcolor{keywordflow}{return} \textcolor{keyword}{reinterpret\_cast<}\mbox{\hyperlink{classT}{T}}*\textcolor{keyword}{>}(}
\DoxyCodeLine{      wrapper-\/>\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Object_a435f68bb7ef0f64dd522c5c910682448}{GetAlignedPointerFromInternalField}}(offset));}
\DoxyCodeLine{\}}
\DoxyCodeLine{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keyword}{class }CustomEmbedderType \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{ \textcolor{keyword}{public}:}
\DoxyCodeLine{  \textcolor{comment}{// Returns the raw C object from a wrapper JS object.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{  \textcolor{keyword}{static} CustomEmbedderType* Unwrap(\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{v8::Local<v8::Object>}} wrapper) \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{keywordflow}{return} GetInternalField<CustomEmbedderType,}
\DoxyCodeLine{                            kV8EmbedderWrapperObjectIndex>(wrapper);}
\DoxyCodeLine{  \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{  \textcolor{keyword}{static} \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} FastMethod(\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{v8::Local<v8::Object>}} receiver\_obj, \textcolor{keywordtype}{int} param) \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{    CustomEmbedderType* receiver = \textcolor{keyword}{static\_cast<}CustomEmbedderType*\textcolor{keyword}{>}(}
\DoxyCodeLine{      receiver\_obj-\/>\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Object_a435f68bb7ef0f64dd522c5c910682448}{GetAlignedPointerFromInternalField}}(}

\DoxyCodeLine{}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{comment}{// Type checks are already done by the optimized code.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{comment}{// Then call some performance-\/critical method like:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{comment}{// receiver-\/>Method(param);}}
\DoxyCodeLine{  \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{}
\DoxyCodeLine{  \textcolor{keyword}{static} \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} SlowMethod(}

\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{comment}{// TODO: Do type checks and extract \{param\}.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{    receiver-\/>Method(param);}
\DoxyCodeLine{  \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\};}
\DoxyCodeLine{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{comment}{// TODO(mslekova): Clean-\/up these constants}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{comment}{// The constants kV8EmbedderWrapperTypeIndex and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{comment}{// kV8EmbedderWrapperObjectIndex describe the offsets for the type info}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{comment}{// struct and the native object, when expressed as internal field indices}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{comment}{// within a JSObject. The existance of this helper function assumes that}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{comment}{// all embedder objects have their JSObject-\/side type info at the same}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{comment}{// offset, but this is not a limitation of the API itself. For a detailed}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{comment}{// use case, see the third example.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keyword}{static} constexpr \textcolor{keywordtype}{int} kV8EmbedderWrapperTypeIndex = 0;}

\DoxyCodeLine{}

\DoxyCodeLine{\}}

\end{DoxyCode}


For instance if \{object\} is exposed via a global \char`\"{}obj\char`\"{} variable, one could write in JS\+: function hot\+\_\+func() \{ obj.\+method(42); \} and once \{hot\+\_\+func\} gets optimized, Custom\+Embedder\+Type\+::\+Fast\+Method will be called instead of the slow version, with the following arguments\+: receiver \+:= the \{embedder\+\_\+object\} from above param \+:= 42

Currently supported return types\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item void
\item bool
\item int32\+\_\+t
\item uint32\+\_\+t
\item float32\+\_\+t
\item float64\+\_\+t Currently supported argument types\+:
\end{DoxyItemize}

pointer to an embedder type
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Java\+Script array of primitive types
\item bool
\item int32\+\_\+t
\item uint32\+\_\+t
\item int64\+\_\+t
\item uint64\+\_\+t
\item float32\+\_\+t
\item float64\+\_\+t
\end{DoxyItemize}

The 64-\/bit integer types currently have the IDL (unsigned) long long semantics\+: \href{https://heycam.github.io/webidl/\#abstract-opdef-converttoint}{\texttt{ https\+://heycam.\+github.\+io/webidl/\#abstract-\/opdef-\/converttoint}} In the future we\textquotesingle{}ll extend the API to also provide conversions from/to \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1BigInt}{Big\+Int}} to preserve full precision. The floating point types currently have the IDL (unrestricted) semantics, which is the only one used by Web\+GL. We plan to add support also for restricted floats/doubles, similarly to the \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1BigInt}{Big\+Int}} conversion policies. We also differ from the specific NaN bit pattern that Web\+IDL prescribes (\href{https://heycam.github.io/webidl/\#es-unrestricted-float}{\texttt{ https\+://heycam.\+github.\+io/webidl/\#es-\/unrestricted-\/float}}) in that Blink passes NaN values as-\/is, i.\+e. doesn\textquotesingle{}t normalize them.

To be supported types\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Typed\+Arrays and Array\+Buffers
\item arrays of embedder types
\end{DoxyItemize}

The API offers a limited support for function overloads\+:


\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keywordtype}{void} FastMethod\_2Args(\textcolor{keywordtype}{int} param, \textcolor{keywordtype}{bool} another\_param);}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keywordtype}{void} FastMethod\_3Args(\textcolor{keywordtype}{int} param, \textcolor{keywordtype}{bool} another\_param, \textcolor{keywordtype}{int} third\_param);}
\DoxyCodeLine{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1CFunction}{v8::CFunction}} fast\_method\_2args\_c\_func =}
\DoxyCodeLine{     MakeV8CFunction(FastMethod\_2Args);}
\DoxyCodeLine{\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1CFunction}{v8::CFunction}} fast\_method\_3args\_c\_func =}
\DoxyCodeLine{     MakeV8CFunction(FastMethod\_3Args);}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1CFunction}{v8::CFunction}} fast\_method\_overloads[] = \{fast\_method\_2args\_c\_func,}
\DoxyCodeLine{                                               fast\_method\_3args\_c\_func\};}
\DoxyCodeLine{Local<v8::FunctionTemplate> method\_template =}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1FunctionTemplate_a6afdb4449a1158184c134e229d21b443}{v8::FunctionTemplate::NewWithCFunctionOverloads}}(}
\DoxyCodeLine{        isolate, SlowCallback, data, signature, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_1_1internal_afa9ea55d792121fba92b4cfc8ef8c9d7}{length}},}
\DoxyCodeLine{        constructor\_behavior, side\_effect\_type,}
\DoxyCodeLine{        \{fast\_method\_overloads, 2\});}

\end{DoxyCode}


In this example a single \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1FunctionTemplate}{Function\+Template}} is associated to multiple C++ functions. The overload resolution is currently only based on the number of arguments passed in a call. For example, if this method\+\_\+template is registered with a wrapper JS object as described above, a call with two arguments\+: obj.\+method(42, true); will result in a fast call to Fast\+Method\+\_\+2\+Args, while a call with three or more arguments\+: obj.\+method(42, true, 11); will result in a fast call to Fast\+Method\+\_\+3\+Args. Instead a call with less than two arguments, like\+: obj.\+method(42); would not result in a fast call but would fall back to executing the associated Slow\+Callback.

C++11 embedders can use STL containers with \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Global}{Global}} values, but pre-\/\+C++11 does not support the required move semantic and hence may want these container classes.

This header provides access to information about the value serializer at compile time, without declaring or defining any symbols that require linking to \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1V8}{V8}}.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily using \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_a36a9049250ff9d86fc32ae16f3723a6e}{v8\+::\+Host\+Create\+Shadow\+Realm\+Context\+Callback}} = typedef \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1MaybeLocal}{Maybe\+Local}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Context}{Context}}$>$ ($\ast$)(\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{Local}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Context}{Context}}$>$ initiator\+\_\+context)}



Host\+Create\+Shadow\+Realm\+Context\+Callback is called each time a Shadow\+Realm is being constructed in the initiator\+\_\+context. 

The method combines \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Context}{Context}} creation and implementation defined abstract operation Host\+Initialize\+Shadow\+Realm into one.

The embedder should use \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Context_a11648311890e6127d92335fc438b8211}{v8\+::\+Context\+::\+New}} or \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Context}{v8\+::\+Context}}\+:New\+From\+Snapshot to create a new context. If the creation fails, the embedder must propagate that exception by returning an empty \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1MaybeLocal}{Maybe\+Local}}. 

Definition at line 446 of file v8-\/callbacks.\+h.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_a2acda7f6c689246cd18f0f00feac7d41}\label{namespacev8_a2acda7f6c689246cd18f0f00feac7d41}} 
\index{v8@{v8}!HostImportModuleDynamicallyCallback@{HostImportModuleDynamicallyCallback}}
\index{HostImportModuleDynamicallyCallback@{HostImportModuleDynamicallyCallback}!v8@{v8}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{HostImportModuleDynamicallyCallback}{HostImportModuleDynamicallyCallback}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily using \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_a2acda7f6c689246cd18f0f00feac7d41}{v8\+::\+Host\+Import\+Module\+Dynamically\+Callback}} = typedef \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1MaybeLocal}{Maybe\+Local}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Promise}{Promise}}$>$ ($\ast$)( \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{Local}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Context}{Context}}$>$ context, \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{Local}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Data}{Data}}$>$ host\+\_\+defined\+\_\+options, \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{Local}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Value}{Value}}$>$ resource\+\_\+name, \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{Local}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1String}{String}}$>$ specifier, \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{Local}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1FixedArray}{Fixed\+Array}}$>$ import\+\_\+attributes)}



Host\+Import\+Module\+Dynamically\+Callback is called when we require the embedder to load a module. 

This is used as part of the dynamic import syntax.

The referrer contains metadata about the script/module that calls import.

The specifier is the name of the module that should be imported.

The import\+\_\+attributes are import attributes for this request in the form\+: \mbox{[}key1, value1, key2, value2, ...\mbox{]} where the keys and values are of type \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1String}{v8\+::\+String}}. Note, unlike the \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1FixedArray}{Fixed\+Array}} passed to Resolve\+Module\+Callback and returned from \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1ModuleRequest_a619f8b47705c915325ffa5c47a2305d8}{Module\+Request\+::\+Get\+Import\+Attributes()}}, this array does not contain the source Locations of the attributes.

The embedder must compile, instantiate, evaluate the \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Module}{Module}}, and obtain its namespace object.

The \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Promise}{Promise}} returned from this function is forwarded to userland Java\+Script. The embedder must resolve this promise with the module namespace object. In case of an exception, the embedder must reject this promise with the exception. If the promise creation itself fails (e.\+g. due to stack overflow), the embedder must propagate that exception by returning an empty \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1MaybeLocal}{Maybe\+Local}}. 

Definition at line 368 of file v8-\/callbacks.\+h.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_a081735ca388ba2e07e8b11552850c96f}\label{namespacev8_a081735ca388ba2e07e8b11552850c96f}} 
\index{v8@{v8}!HostImportModuleWithPhaseDynamicallyCallback@{HostImportModuleWithPhaseDynamicallyCallback}}
\index{HostImportModuleWithPhaseDynamicallyCallback@{HostImportModuleWithPhaseDynamicallyCallback}!v8@{v8}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{HostImportModuleWithPhaseDynamicallyCallback}{HostImportModuleWithPhaseDynamicallyCallback}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily using \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_a081735ca388ba2e07e8b11552850c96f}{v8\+::\+Host\+Import\+Module\+With\+Phase\+Dynamically\+Callback}} = typedef \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1MaybeLocal}{Maybe\+Local}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Promise}{Promise}}$>$ ($\ast$)( \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{Local}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Context}{Context}}$>$ context, \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{Local}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Data}{Data}}$>$ host\+\_\+defined\+\_\+options, \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{Local}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Value}{Value}}$>$ resource\+\_\+name, \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{Local}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1String}{String}}$>$ specifier, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_aefa7213d04d46fe1d92221757c4ad10a}{Module\+Import\+Phase}} phase, \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{Local}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1FixedArray}{Fixed\+Array}}$>$ import\+\_\+attributes)}



Host\+Import\+Module\+With\+Phase\+Dynamically\+Callback is called when we require the embedder to load a module with a specific phase. 

This is used as part of the dynamic import syntax.

The referrer contains metadata about the script/module that calls import.

The specifier is the name of the module that should be imported.

The phase is the phase of the import requested.

The import\+\_\+attributes are import attributes for this request in the form\+: \mbox{[}key1, value1, key2, value2, ...\mbox{]} where the keys and values are of type \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1String}{v8\+::\+String}}. Note, unlike the \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1FixedArray}{Fixed\+Array}} passed to Resolve\+Module\+Callback and returned from \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1ModuleRequest_a619f8b47705c915325ffa5c47a2305d8}{Module\+Request\+::\+Get\+Import\+Attributes()}}, this array does not contain the source Locations of the attributes.

The \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Promise}{Promise}} returned from this function is forwarded to userland Java\+Script. The embedder must resolve this promise according to the phase requested\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item For \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_aefa7213d04d46fe1d92221757c4ad10aac1c0088a4e8654d4dc2f5fdf247381b0}{Module\+Import\+Phase\+::k\+Source}}, the promise must be resolved with a compiled Module\+Source object, or rejected with a Syntax\+Error if the module does not support source representation.
\item For \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_aefa7213d04d46fe1d92221757c4ad10aa346bc9a934c8efdaded7eb6f74d86d0f}{Module\+Import\+Phase\+::k\+Evaluation}}, the promise must be resolved with a Module\+Namespace object of a module that has been compiled, instantiated, and evaluated.
\end{DoxyItemize}

In case of an exception, the embedder must reject this promise with the exception. If the promise creation itself fails (e.\+g. due to stack overflow), the embedder must propagate that exception by returning an empty \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1MaybeLocal}{Maybe\+Local}}.

This callback is still experimental and is only invoked for source phase imports. 

Definition at line 409 of file v8-\/callbacks.\+h.

Host\+Initialize\+Import\+Meta\+Object\+Callback is called the first time import.\+meta is accessed for a module. 

Subsequent access will reuse the same value.

The method combines two implementation-\/defined abstract operations into one\+: Host\+Get\+Import\+Meta\+Properties and Host\+Finalize\+Import\+Meta.

The embedder should use \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Object_a826077e71c717f94deeeaa9bfca1b249}{v8\+::\+Object\+::\+Create\+Data\+Property}} to add properties on the meta object.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_a434a6b37e76938f20828f4c1d2d9a194}\label{namespacev8_a434a6b37e76938f20828f4c1d2d9a194}}

\index{NamedPropertyDefinerCallback@{NamedPropertyDefinerCallback}!v8@{v8}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{NamedPropertyDefinerCallback}{NamedPropertyDefinerCallback}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily using \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_a434a6b37e76938f20828f4c1d2d9a194}{v8\+::\+Named\+Property\+Definer\+Callback}} = typedef \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_af6fda56e02b3f46cded582193435f3a7}{Intercepted}} ($\ast$)(\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{Local}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Name}{Name}}$>$ property, const \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1PropertyDescriptor}{Property\+Descriptor}}\& desc, const \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1PropertyCallbackInfo}{Property\+Callback\+Info}}$<$void$>$\& info)}



Interceptor for define\+Property requests on an object. 

If the interceptor handles the request (i.\+e. the property should not be looked up beyond the interceptor or in case an exception was thrown) it should return {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_af6fda56e02b3f46cded582193435f3a7a1ea590aa4a64767508460736ac0edaa9}{Intercepted\+::k\+Yes}}}. If the interceptor does not handle the request it must return {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_af6fda56e02b3f46cded582193435f3a7a8cc8e60acfa3ae6089df773013fd73a2}{Intercepted\+::k\+No}}} and it must not produce side effects.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em property} & The name of the property for which the request was intercepted. \\
\hline
{\em desc} & The property descriptor which is used to define the property if the request is not intercepted. \\
\hline
{\em info} & Information about the intercepted request, such as isolate, receiver, return value, or whether running in `\textquotesingle{}use strict'{\ttfamily mode. See}Property\+Callback\+Info\`{}.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
See also {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1ObjectTemplate_a3d5666f1e9b0f46df6b4dbb7cfbb6114}{Object\+Template\+::\+Set\+Handler}}}.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_ae1c48fbc7c012a3af01d8ce505b24f86}\label{namespacev8_ae1c48fbc7c012a3af01d8ce505b24f86}} 
\index{v8@{v8}!NamedPropertyDeleterCallback@{NamedPropertyDeleterCallback}}
\index{NamedPropertyDeleterCallback@{NamedPropertyDeleterCallback}!v8@{v8}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{NamedPropertyDeleterCallback}{NamedPropertyDeleterCallback}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily using \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_ae1c48fbc7c012a3af01d8ce505b24f86}{v8\+::\+Named\+Property\+Deleter\+Callback}} = typedef \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_af6fda56e02b3f46cded582193435f3a7}{Intercepted}} ($\ast$)( \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{Local}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Name}{Name}}$>$ property, const \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1PropertyCallbackInfo}{Property\+Callback\+Info}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Boolean}{Boolean}}$>$\& info)}



Interceptor for delete requests on an object. 

If the interceptor handles the request (i.\+e. the property should not be looked up beyond the interceptor or in case an exception was thrown) it should
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item (optionally) use {\ttfamily info.\+Get\+Return\+Value().Set()} to set to a \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Boolean}{Boolean}} value indicating whether the property deletion was successful or not,
\item return {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_af6fda56e02b3f46cded582193435f3a7a1ea590aa4a64767508460736ac0edaa9}{Intercepted\+::k\+Yes}}}. If the interceptor does not handle the request it must return {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_af6fda56e02b3f46cded582193435f3a7a8cc8e60acfa3ae6089df773013fd73a2}{Intercepted\+::k\+No}}} and it must not produce side effects.
\end{DoxyItemize}


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em property} & The name of the property for which the request was intercepted. \\
\hline
{\em info} & Information about the intercepted request, such as isolate, receiver, return value, or whether running in `\textquotesingle{}use strict'{\ttfamily mode. See}Property\+Callback\+Info\`{}.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
If you need to mimic the behavior of {\ttfamily delete}, i.\+e., throw in strict mode instead of returning false, use {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_1_1internal_a8a792f15e5229e11d374807a9c7a5ad5}{info.\+Should\+Throw\+On\+Error()}}} to determine if you are in strict mode.
\end{DoxyNote}
See also {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1ObjectTemplate_a3d5666f1e9b0f46df6b4dbb7cfbb6114}{Object\+Template\+::\+Set\+Handler}}.}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_a2d60f33ee7bc694e918707cbf836138f}\label{namespacev8_a2d60f33ee7bc694e918707cbf836138f}} 
\index{v8@{v8}!NamedPropertyDescriptorCallback@{NamedPropertyDescriptorCallback}}
\index{NamedPropertyDescriptorCallback@{NamedPropertyDescriptorCallback}!v8@{v8}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{NamedPropertyDescriptorCallback}{NamedPropertyDescriptorCallback}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily using \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_a2d60f33ee7bc694e918707cbf836138f}{v8\+::\+Named\+Property\+Descriptor\+Callback}} = typedef \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_af6fda56e02b3f46cded582193435f3a7}{Intercepted}} ($\ast$)( \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{Local}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Name}{Name}}$>$ property, const \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1PropertyCallbackInfo}{Property\+Callback\+Info}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Value}{Value}}$>$\& info)}



Interceptor for get\+Own\+Property\+Descriptor requests on an object. 

If the interceptor handles the request (i.\+e. the property should not be looked up beyond the interceptor or in case an exception was thrown) it should
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item (optionally) use {\ttfamily info.\+Get\+Return\+Value().Set()} to set the return value which must be object that can be converted to a \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1PropertyDescriptor}{Property\+Descriptor}} (for example, a value returned by {\ttfamily v8\+::\+Object\+::get\+Own\+Property\+Descriptor}),
\item return {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_af6fda56e02b3f46cded582193435f3a7a1ea590aa4a64767508460736ac0edaa9}{Intercepted\+::k\+Yes}}}. If the interceptor does not handle the request it must return {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_af6fda56e02b3f46cded582193435f3a7a8cc8e60acfa3ae6089df773013fd73a2}{Intercepted\+::k\+No}}} and it must not produce side effects.
\end{DoxyItemize}


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em property} & The name of the property for which the request was intercepted. \textbackslash{}info Information about the intercepted request, such as isolate, receiver, return value, or whether running in `\textquotesingle{}use strict'{\ttfamily mode. See}Property\+Callback\+Info\`{}.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
If Get\+Own\+Property\+Descriptor is intercepted, it will always return true, i.\+e., indicate that the property was found.
\end{DoxyNote}
See also {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1ObjectTemplate_a3d5666f1e9b0f46df6b4dbb7cfbb6114}{Object\+Template\+::\+Set\+Handler}}}.

Definition at line 184 of file v8-\/template.\+h.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_ace09ca9c098de6cb019d09a988d4c897}\label{namespacev8_ace09ca9c098de6cb019d09a988d4c897}} 
\index{v8@{v8}!NamedPropertyQueryCallback@{NamedPropertyQueryCallback}}
\index{NamedPropertyQueryCallback@{NamedPropertyQueryCallback}!v8@{v8}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{NamedPropertyQueryCallback}{NamedPropertyQueryCallback}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily using \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_ace09ca9c098de6cb019d09a988d4c897}{v8\+::\+Named\+Property\+Query\+Callback}} = typedef \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_af6fda56e02b3f46cded582193435f3a7}{Intercepted}} ($\ast$)( \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{Local}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Name}{Name}}$>$ property, const \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1PropertyCallbackInfo}{Property\+Callback\+Info}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Integer}{Integer}}$>$\& info)}



Intercepts all requests that query the attributes of the property, e.\+g., get\+Own\+Property\+Descriptor(), property\+Is\+Enumerable(), and define\+Property(). 

If the interceptor handles the request (i.\+e. the property should not be looked up beyond the interceptor or in case an exception was thrown) it should
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item (optionally) use {\ttfamily info.\+Get\+Return\+Value().Set()} to set to an \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Integer}{Integer}} value encoding a {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_a05f25f935e108a1ea2d150e274602b87}{v8\+::\+Property\+Attribute}}} bits,
\item return {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_af6fda56e02b3f46cded582193435f3a7a1ea590aa4a64767508460736ac0edaa9}{Intercepted\+::k\+Yes}}}. If the interceptor does not handle the request it must return {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_af6fda56e02b3f46cded582193435f3a7a8cc8e60acfa3ae6089df773013fd73a2}{Intercepted\+::k\+No}}} and it must not produce side effects.
\end{DoxyItemize}


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em property} & The name of the property for which the request was intercepted. \\
\hline
{\em info} & Information about the intercepted request, such as isolate, receiver, return value, or whether running in `\textquotesingle{}use strict'{\ttfamily mode. See}Property\+Callback\+Info\`{}.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
Some functions query the property attributes internally, even though they do not return the attributes. For example, {\ttfamily has\+Own\+Property()} can trigger this interceptor depending on the state of the object.
\end{DoxyNote}
See also {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1ObjectTemplate_a3d5666f1e9b0f46df6b4dbb7cfbb6114}{Object\+Template\+::\+Set\+Handler}}.} 

Definition at line 256 of file v8-\/template.\+h.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_a147fed9d8eed6e9e9a4944117e232d00}\label{namespacev8_a147fed9d8eed6e9e9a4944117e232d00}} 
\index{v8@{v8}!NamedPropertySetterCallback@{NamedPropertySetterCallback}}
\index{NamedPropertySetterCallback@{NamedPropertySetterCallback}!v8@{v8}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{NamedPropertySetterCallback}{NamedPropertySetterCallback}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily using \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_a147fed9d8eed6e9e9a4944117e232d00}{v8\+::\+Named\+Property\+Setter\+Callback}} = typedef \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_af6fda56e02b3f46cded582193435f3a7}{Intercepted}} ($\ast$)(\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{Local}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Name}{Name}}$>$ property, \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{Local}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Value}{Value}}$>$ value, const \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1PropertyCallbackInfo}{Property\+Callback\+Info}}$<$void$>$\& info)}



Interceptor for set requests on an object. 

If the interceptor handles the request (i.\+e. the property should not be looked up beyond the interceptor or in case an exception was thrown) it should return {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_af6fda56e02b3f46cded582193435f3a7a1ea590aa4a64767508460736ac0edaa9}{Intercepted\+::k\+Yes}}}. If the interceptor does not handle the request it must return {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_af6fda56e02b3f46cded582193435f3a7a8cc8e60acfa3ae6089df773013fd73a2}{Intercepted\+::k\+No}}} and it must not produce side effects.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em property} & The name of the property for which the request was intercepted. \\
\hline
{\em value} & The value which the property will have if the request is not intercepted. \\
\hline
{\em info} & Information about the intercepted request, such as isolate, receiver, return value, or whether running in `\textquotesingle{}use strict'{\ttfamily mode. See}Property\+Callback\+Info\`{}.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
See also {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1ObjectTemplate_a3d5666f1e9b0f46df6b4dbb7cfbb6114}{Object\+Template\+::\+Set\+Handler}}.}

Definition at line 30 of file v8-\/profiler.\+h.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_aa1fc7d6f7736e8256fc03c4b3ebaf6eb}\label{namespacev8_aa1fc7d6f7736e8256fc03c4b3ebaf6eb}} 
\index{v8@{v8}!NearHeapLimitCallback@{NearHeapLimitCallback}}
\index{NearHeapLimitCallback@{NearHeapLimitCallback}!v8@{v8}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{NearHeapLimitCallback}{NearHeapLimitCallback}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily using \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_aa1fc7d6f7736e8256fc03c4b3ebaf6eb}{v8\+::\+Near\+Heap\+Limit\+Callback}} = typedef size\+\_\+t ($\ast$)(void$\ast$ data, size\+\_\+t current\+\_\+heap\+\_\+limit, size\+\_\+t initial\+\_\+heap\+\_\+limit)}



This callback is invoked when the heap size is close to the heap limit and \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1V8}{V8}} is likely to abort with out-\/of-\/memory error. 

The callback can extend the heap limit by returning a value that is greater than the current\+\_\+heap\+\_\+limit. The initial heap limit is the limit that was set after heap setup.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_a98679679b01cacd67f2c4b401ef197af}\label{namespacev8_a98679679b01cacd67f2c4b401ef197af}} 
\index{v8@{v8}!ReturnAddressLocationResolver@{ReturnAddressLocationResolver}}
\index{ReturnAddressLocationResolver@{ReturnAddressLocationResolver}!v8@{v8}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{ReturnAddressLocationResolver}{ReturnAddressLocationResolver}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily using \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_a98679679b01cacd67f2c4b401ef197af}{v8\+::\+Return\+Address\+Location\+Resolver}} = typedef \mbox{\hyperlink{classuintptr__t}{uintptr\+\_\+t}} ($\ast$)(\mbox{\hyperlink{classuintptr__t}{uintptr\+\_\+t}} return\+\_\+addr\+\_\+location)}



Return\+Address\+Location\+Resolver is used as a callback function when \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8}{v8}} is resolving the location of a return address on the stack. 

Profilers that change the return address on the stack can use this to resolve the stack location to wherever the profiler stashed the original return address.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em return\+\_\+addr\+\_\+location} & A location on stack where a machine return address resides. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Either return\+\_\+addr\+\_\+location, or else a pointer to the profiler\textquotesingle{}s copy of the original return address.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
The resolver function must not cause garbage collection. 
\end{DoxyNote}

\index{v8@{v8}!BlockingType@{BlockingType}}
\index{BlockingType@{BlockingType}!v8@{v8}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{BlockingType}{BlockingType}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily enum \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_abd498c5a2b655d1b83c730aa38ad1bfa}{v8\+::\+Blocking\+Type}}\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [strong]}}



A \char`\"{}blocking call\char`\"{} refers to any call that causes the calling thread to wait off-\/\+CPU. 

It includes but is not limited to calls that wait on synchronous file I/O operations\+: read or write a file from disk, interact with a pipe or a socket, rename or delete a file, enumerate files in a directory, etc. Acquiring a low contention lock is not considered a blocking call. Blocking\+Type indicates the likelihood that a blocking call will actually block. \begin{DoxyEnumFields}{Enumerator}
\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{kMayBlock@{kMayBlock}!v8@{v8}}\index{v8@{v8}!kMayBlock@{kMayBlock}}}\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_abd498c5a2b655d1b83c730aa38ad1bfaaec6621c4e7d287f76d6959cf112c8fdc}\label{namespacev8_abd498c5a2b655d1b83c730aa38ad1bfaaec6621c4e7d287f76d6959cf112c8fdc}} 
k\+May\+Block&\\

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_aaa20110c92e8833826af037fe31401b2}\label{namespacev8_aaa20110c92e8833826af037fe31401b2}} 
\index{v8@{v8}!CppHeapPointerTag@{CppHeapPointerTag}}
\index{CppHeapPointerTag@{CppHeapPointerTag}!v8@{v8}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{CppHeapPointerTag}{CppHeapPointerTag}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily enum \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_aaa20110c92e8833826af037fe31401b2}{v8\+::\+Cpp\+Heap\+Pointer\+Tag}} \+: uint16\+\_\+t\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [strong]}}



A pointer tag used for wrapping and unwrapping {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1CppHeap}{Cpp\+Heap}}} pointers as used with JS API wrapper objects that rely on {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Object_a657610a5db05d2673cb8c4ad855a1c6e}{v8\+::\+Object\+::\+Wrap()}}} and {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Object_ac9812adb53766f0410d3275c53b49cfa}{v8\+::\+Object\+::\+Unwrap()}}}. 

The Cpp\+Heap\+Pointers use a range-\/based type checking scheme, where on access to a pointer, the actual type of the pointer is checked to be within a specified range of types. This allows supporting type hierarchies, where a type check for a supertype must succeed for any subtype.

The tag is currently in practice limited to 15 bits since it needs to fit together with a marking bit into the unused parts of a pointer. \begin{DoxyEnumFields}{Enumerator}
\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{kFirstTag@{kFirstTag}!v8@{v8}}\index{v8@{v8}!kFirstTag@{kFirstTag}}}\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_aaa20110c92e8833826af037fe31401b2a1af3cb02e2f65a612a6484d2129846ca}\label{namespacev8_aaa20110c92e8833826af037fe31401b2a1af3cb02e2f65a612a6484d2129846ca}} 
k\+First\+Tag&\\
\hline

\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{kNullTag@{kNullTag}!v8@{v8}}\index{v8@{v8}!kNullTag@{kNullTag}}}\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_aaa20110c92e8833826af037fe31401b2a71f8acb0cee963152c7d8fade5c50745}\label{namespacev8_aaa20110c92e8833826af037fe31401b2a71f8acb0cee963152c7d8fade5c50745}} 
k\+Null\+Tag&\\
\hline

\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{kDefaultTag@{kDefaultTag}!v8@{v8}}\index{v8@{v8}!kDefaultTag@{kDefaultTag}}}\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_aaa20110c92e8833826af037fe31401b2ad76a59263f4a4c7cd42f07c8196e160e}\label{namespacev8_aaa20110c92e8833826af037fe31401b2ad76a59263f4a4c7cd42f07c8196e160e}} 
k\+Default\+Tag&The lower type ids are reserved for the embedder to assign. For that, the main requirement is that all (transitive) child classes of a given parent class have type ids in the same range, and that there are no unrelated types in that range. For example, given the following type hierarchy\+: \begin{DoxyVerb}     A     F
    / \
   B   E
  / \
 C   D
\end{DoxyVerb}
 a potential type id assignment that satistifes these requirements is \{C\+: 0, D\+: 1, B\+: 2, A\+: 3, E\+: 4, F\+: 5\}. With that, the type check for type A would check for the range \mbox{[}0, 4\mbox{]}, while the check for B would check range \mbox{[}0, 2\mbox{]}, and for F it would simply check \mbox{[}5, 5\mbox{]}.

In addition, there is an option for performance tweaks\+: if the size of the type range corresponding to a supertype is a power of two and starts at a power of two (e.\+g. \mbox{[}0x100, 0x13f\mbox{]}), then the compiler can often optimize the type check to use even fewer instructions (essentially replace a AND + SUB with a single AND). \\
\hline

\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{kZappedEntryTag@{kZappedEntryTag}!v8@{v8}}\index{v8@{v8}!kZappedEntryTag@{kZappedEntryTag}}}\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_aaa20110c92e8833826af037fe31401b2a5587694029787ff80c31a4bb75a4f5b1}\label{namespacev8_aaa20110c92e8833826af037fe31401b2a5587694029787ff80c31a4bb75a4f5b1}} 
k\+Zapped\+Entry\+Tag&\\

k\+Evacuation\+Entry\+Tag&\\
\hline

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_a247c37a849f4d6c293b9b16e94e1944b}\label{namespacev8_a247c37a849f4d6c293b9b16e94e1944b}} 
\index{v8@{v8}!GCCallbackFlags@{GCCallbackFlags}}
\index{GCCallbackFlags@{GCCallbackFlags}!v8@{v8}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{GCCallbackFlags}{GCCallbackFlags}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily enum \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_a247c37a849f4d6c293b9b16e94e1944b}{v8\+::\+GCCallback\+Flags}}}



GCCallback\+Flags is used to notify additional information about the GC callback. 


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item k\+GCCallback\+Flag\+Construct\+Retained\+Object\+Infos\+: The GC callback is for constructing retained object infos.
\item k\+GCCallback\+Flag\+Forced\+: The GC callback is for a forced GC for testing.
\item k\+GCCallback\+Flag\+Synchronous\+Phantom\+Callback\+Processing\+: The GC callback is called synchronously without getting posted to an idle task.
\item k\+GCCallback\+Flag\+Collect\+All\+Available\+Garbage\+: The GC callback is called in a phase where \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1V8}{V8}} is trying to collect all available garbage (e.\+g., handling a low memory notification).
\item k\+GCCallback\+Schedule\+Idle\+Garbage\+Collection\+: The GC callback is called to trigger an idle garbage collection. 
\end{DoxyItemize}\begin{DoxyEnumFields}{Enumerator}
\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{kNoGCCallbackFlags@{kNoGCCallbackFlags}!v8@{v8}}\index{v8@{v8}!kNoGCCallbackFlags@{kNoGCCallbackFlags}}}\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_a247c37a849f4d6c293b9b16e94e1944babf7ad124c420ea94357f9472256ca74e}\label{namespacev8_a247c37a849f4d6c293b9b16e94e1944babf7ad124c420ea94357f9472256ca74e}} 
k\+No\+GCCallback\+Flags&\\
\hline

\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{kGCCallbackFlagConstructRetainedObjectInfos@{kGCCallbackFlagConstructRetainedObjectInfos}!v8@{v8}}\index{v8@{v8}!kGCCallbackFlagConstructRetainedObjectInfos@{kGCCallbackFlagConstructRetainedObjectInfos}}}\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_a247c37a849f4d6c293b9b16e94e1944ba462b0367d97a6c13097b69e1d7a807da}\label{namespacev8_a247c37a849f4d6c293b9b16e94e1944ba462b0367d97a6c13097b69e1d7a807da}}

\index{v8@{v8}!GCType@{GCType}}
\index{GCType@{GCType}!v8@{v8}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{GCType}{GCType}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily enum \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_ac109d6f27e0c0f9ef4e98bcf7a806cf2}{v8\+::\+GCType}}}



Applications can register callback functions which will be called before and after certain garbage collection operations. 

Allocations are not allowed in the callback functions, you therefore cannot manipulate objects (set or delete properties for example) since it is possible such operations will result in the allocation of objects. Controls how promptly a memory measurement request is executed. 

By default the measurement is folded with the next scheduled GC which may happen after a while and is forced after some timeout. The k\+Eager mode starts incremental GC right away and is useful for testing. The k\+Lazy mode does not force GC. \begin{DoxyEnumFields}{Enumerator}

Memory pressure level for the Memory\+Pressure\+Notification. 

k\+None hints \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1V8}{V8}} that there is no memory pressure. k\+Moderate hints \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1V8}{V8}} to speed up incremental garbage collection at the cost of of higher latency due to garbage collection pauses. k\+Critical hints \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1V8}{V8}} to free memory as soon as possible. Garbage collection pauses at this level will be large. \begin{DoxyEnumFields}{Enumerator}

\index{v8@{v8}!PromiseHookType@{PromiseHookType}}
\index{PromiseHookType@{PromiseHookType}!v8@{v8}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{PromiseHookType}{PromiseHookType}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily enum \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_afe9d9e16c02074ac8482a8f09e19d5cc}{v8\+::\+Promise\+Hook\+Type}}\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [strong]}}



Promise\+Hook with type k\+Init is called when a new promise is created. 

When a new promise is created as part of the chain in the case of Promise.\+then or in the intermediate promises created by \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Promise}{Promise}}.\{race, all\}/\+Async\+Function\+Await, we pass the parent promise otherwise we pass undefined.

Promise\+Hook with type k\+Resolve is called at the beginning of resolve or reject function defined by Create\+Resolving\+Functions.

Promise\+Hook with type k\+Before is called at the beginning of the Promise\+Reaction\+Job.

Promise\+Hook with type k\+After is called right at the end of the Promise\+Reaction\+Job. \begin{DoxyEnumFields}{Enumerator}
\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{kInit@{kInit}!v8@{v8}}\index{v8@{v8}!kInit@{kInit}}}\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_afe9d9e16c02074ac8482a8f09e19d5ccab217b1cb58a6ee4ef35a6c84cf367659}\label{namespacev8_afe9d9e16c02074ac8482a8f09e19d5ccab217b1cb58a6ee4ef35a6c84cf367659}}

\index{v8@{v8}!SideEffectType@{SideEffectType}}
\index{SideEffectType@{SideEffectType}!v8@{v8}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{SideEffectType}{SideEffectType}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily enum \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_a29711319c2b9fc7716d65faee2f7b9cb}{v8\+::\+Side\+Effect\+Type}}\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [strong]}}



Options for marking whether callbacks may trigger JS-\/observable side effects. 

Side-\/effect-\/free callbacks are allowlisted during debug evaluation with throw\+On\+Side\+Effect. It applies when calling a \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Function}{Function}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1FunctionTemplate}{Function\+Template}}, or an Accessor callback. For Interceptors, please see Property\+Handler\+Flags\textquotesingle{}s k\+Has\+No\+Side\+Effect. Callbacks that only cause side effects to the receiver are allowlisted if invoked on receiver objects that are created within the same debug-\/evaluate call, as these objects are temporary and the side effect does not escape. \begin{DoxyEnumFields}{Enumerator}
\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{kHasSideEffect@{kHasSideEffect}!v8@{v8}}\index{v8@{v8}!kHasSideEffect@{kHasSideEffect}}}\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_a29711319c2b9fc7716d65faee2f7b9cba990e9e01ed66f6917a426b610d20ac46}\label{namespacev8_a29711319c2b9fc7716d65faee2f7b9cba990e9e01ed66f6917a426b610d20ac46}}

k\+User\+Blocking&User blocking tasks are highest priority tasks that block the execution thread (e.\+g. major garbage collection). They must be finished as soon as possible. \\

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_a801e3a2af23e3fdef8b4a728bccbcccf}\label{namespacev8_a801e3a2af23e3fdef8b4a728bccbcccf}} 
\index{v8@{v8}!TryHandleWebAssemblyTrapPosix@{TryHandleWebAssemblyTrapPosix}}
\index{TryHandleWebAssemblyTrapPosix@{TryHandleWebAssemblyTrapPosix}!v8@{v8}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{TryHandleWebAssemblyTrapPosix()}{TryHandleWebAssemblyTrapPosix()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily bool v8\+::\+Try\+Handle\+Web\+Assembly\+Trap\+Posix (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classint}{int}}}]{sig\+\_\+code,  }\item[{siginfo\+\_\+t $\ast$}]{info,  }\item[{void $\ast$}]{context }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



This function determines whether a memory access violation has been an out-\/of-\/bounds memory access in Web\+Assembly. 

If so, it will modify the context parameter and add a return address where the execution can continue after the signal handling, and return true. Otherwise, false will be returned.

The parameters to this function correspond to those passed to a Posix signal handler. Use this function only on Linux and Mac.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em sig\+\_\+code} & The signal code, e.\+g. SIGSEGV. \\
\hline
{\em info} & A pointer to the siginfo\+\_\+t struct provided to the signal handler. \\
\hline
{\em context} & A pointer to a ucontext\+\_\+t struct provided to the signal handler. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_a3686a31962558f552b86653f59e774dd}\label{namespacev8_a3686a31962558f552b86653f59e774dd}} 
\index{v8@{v8}!TryHandleWebAssemblyTrapWindows@{TryHandleWebAssemblyTrapWindows}}
\index{TryHandleWebAssemblyTrapWindows@{TryHandleWebAssemblyTrapWindows}!v8@{v8}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{TryHandleWebAssemblyTrapWindows()}{TryHandleWebAssemblyTrapWindows()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily bool v8\+::\+Try\+Handle\+Web\+Assembly\+Trap\+Windows (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{EXCEPTION\+\_\+\+POINTERS $\ast$}]{exception }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



This function determines whether a memory access violation has been an out-\/of-\/bounds memory access in Web\+Assembly. 

If so, it will modify the exception parameter and add a return address where the execution can continue after the exception handling, and return true. Otherwise the return value will be false.

The parameter to this function corresponds to the one passed to a Windows vectored exception handler. Use this function only on Windows.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em exception} & An EXCEPTION\+\_\+\+POINTERS$\ast$ as provided to the exception handler. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacev8_acfad576b00bc7c0bfc0236ae5ab52b3d}\label{namespacev8_acfad576b00bc7c0bfc0236ae5ab52b3d}} 
\index{v8@{v8}!TryToCopyAndConvertArrayToCppBuffer@{TryToCopyAndConvertArrayToCppBuffer}}
\index{TryToCopyAndConvertArrayToCppBuffer@{TryToCopyAndConvertArrayToCppBuffer}!v8@{v8}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{TryToCopyAndConvertArrayToCppBuffer()}{TryToCopyAndConvertArrayToCppBuffer()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$CType\+Info\+::\+Identifier type\+\_\+info\+\_\+id, typename T $>$ \\
bool \mbox{\hyperlink{v8config_8h_a63258e4bf5dc9fb8c78f881c8405d83b}{V8\+\_\+\+WARN\+\_\+\+UNUSED\+\_\+\+RESULT}} v8\+::\+Try\+To\+Copy\+And\+Convert\+Array\+To\+Cpp\+Buffer (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Local}{Local}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1Array}{Array}} $>$}]{src,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classT}{T}} $\ast$}]{dst,  }\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{max\+\_\+length }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Copies the contents of this Java\+Script array to a C++ buffer with a given max\+\_\+length. 

A \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1CTypeInfo}{CType\+Info}} is passed as an argument, instructing different rules for conversion (e.\+g. restricted float/double). The element type \mbox{\hyperlink{classT}{T}} of the destination array must match the C type corresponding to the \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1CTypeInfo}{CType\+Info}} (specified by CType\+Info\+Traits). If the array length is larger than max\+\_\+length or the array is of unsupported type, the operation will fail, returning false. Generally, an array which contains objects, undefined, null or anything not convertible to the requested destination type, is considered unsupported. The operation returns true on success. {\ttfamily type\+\_\+info} will be used for conversions.
